They do price negotiate here, but don't be too pushy because they can and will push back on you leaving a slight sour taste in your month. Overall, one of the only places around the west bay side you can find what you're looking for.<//text>

< review>
This place has been a staple in Oakland for a really long time, and it is still a great place to kick it on the weekend while in Oakland, if you like a mixed crowd. The couple of times I've been here, the only thing I could find wrong with the layout, is the fact they could use a nice renovation. However, the building is probably an upgrade away from becoming the poor contractors nightmare. What they do have going for them, is a gray staff  attentive to big crowds. The buffet, which consisted of fried fish, grilled chicken, greens, potato salad, and some delicious jiffy mix cornbread  was actually delicious for the setting and bulk cooked. Had a great time here every time I've visited, and seems as though they had live music lady time I went, and two different genre DJ's before that.< /review>

< review>
A friend took me there last Sunday night. It's a small venue for very enjoyable jazz. She knew many of the attendees. Folks were hospitable. I thought the music was excellent. I'm not a jazz buff, but I really  enjoyed the evening. After about an hour of listening to the headline singer, there was an hour of open mic. I really was amazed at their talent I enjoyed them as much as the headliner.

For $10 there was an optional buffet of Soul Food. It looked tasty but not food that I choose to eat. My friend loved it. We parked a short distance away for free in a lot. Personally, I am not comfortable walking in Oakland at night. I would only go with someone, certainly not alone. Oh, I forgot the $10 cover charge. It was worth it. A glass of wine with $7, admittedly, a small glass of wine.Geoffrey, the club owner, was so dear and gracious. The elevator was not working after they had tried to fix it. He was so apologetic. I immediately liked the man.<//review>

<Time>1606697882850<//Time><rating>5</rating>< Review>
Relaxing and pretty place for families of all sorts to come and enjoy. This park is from San Jose's sister city, Okayama-Shi, located in Japan, and everything in here preserves the Japanese serenity and traditional beauty.
What's not beautiful are some Instagram girls and wannabes who come here and hog the small walkways so they can take 470 pictures of themselves under the changing leaves.
Insider tip, parking and entrance are free during Covid, so there are plenty of people visiting this place. The best autumn leaves Kodak moments were between Nov 19-26. Don't forget to walk around the surrounding park and Happy Hallow if you have the time.< /Review>

<user_id>101251283384042316557<//user_id>< name>
Mark Cigler< /name>
<date>1600663161400<//date><rating>5</rating>< review>
The Japanese Friendship Garden
with its diverse landscapes, tall
trees and comforting grass areas
invites young and old families to
relax and explore. Some families set up easy tents just for the day.
Restrooms and tables are open,
BBQs are not.
You will see; birds, turtles, coy, and
and so much more. Amazing
japanese landscapes in San Jose?
Yes it is vivid and true. Visit once
and you will never forget what has
been experienced. Awesome, clean
and very friendly. There is a
peaceful resident crane that moves
elegantly and will fill you with
wonder. Leave a dollar or more in
donation "fountain".<//review>

Took my granddaughters there it was their first visit to the Japanese Friendship Garden. They enjoyed walking around. At this time only one pond is filled with water, the larger ponds are dry. Upon arrival at the Japanese Friendship Garden I quickly realized that there is little to be friends with aside from the concrete. All the pools are drained and devoid of koi. One can only pray that they are still alive... Somewhere. In solidarity I lay my body prone on the gravel floor of the ponds where they once swam so freely. Good plants and vegetation though, I got a few good tree hugs in. It's also fun to gallop on all fours down the dry ravines where the fish and water lilies once fliurished.</text>

< review>
This was once one of my favorite places to visit in San Jose. At one time I would even argue that this was a better place to visit than the one in SF. At this point though it's not really worth even stopping at. Two thirds of the ponds have been dry for years. Yes, I understand this was a result of the sewage flood thanks to San Jose not being able to handle a little rain. I also understand this area wastes money on plenty of things that aren't as important to me, and we are talking several years now.

As bad as all that is, today was the final straw  At some point they taped a sign over their hours to close at 4PM. We didn't realize it until the ranger locked my girlfriend and I in. Some shouted, be we weren't able to understand exactly what was said.  We started walking to the gate to see what was going on, instead we only found it locked. In our escape planning we ran into another couple that was trapped as well.  I guess luckily for all of us the fence is in a similar state of disrepair to the ponds since we were a le to find a bald spot in the barbed wire to make a break for it.<//review>

<userid>113692239181165631637<//userid>< user_name>
Susan Aoki</user_name>
< Time>
1568788002423< /Time>
<rating>5< /rating>< Review>
Beautiful and serene.  A gift from the city of Okayama in Japan during the early 60s.   A rare gem in San Jose, 6.5 acres and you will be transported to a thoughtful place where you are encouraged to be in the moment and relax.  Although the City is repairing the ponds from the flood 2.5 years ago still, the garden is still a haven for animals and beauty.  No fee to enter, parking is about $6 in Senter/Alma lot, and $10 in the lot next to Happy Hollow, free parking if you drive around the stadium area if it's not crowded.  Hours are generally 10am to 5pm, but maybe later - check the website.</Review>

<user_id>109849026903893201606<//user_id><user_name>Jayasimha Nuggehalli</user_name>< Date>

<Rate>5</Rate>< review>
This Japanese Garden is in Kelly Park San Jose. Park is around 6 acres, established in 1965` Entrance to the park is free. However there is a $10 fee for parking. You can also find free street parking near by. Great location for photo shoots or just relax in the garden. Garden has three ponds. Pond under the bridge is Koi pond.

This garden got affected by flood in San Jose, couple of years ago. Now restoration is going on in the garden specially Koi pond. Now the Koi pond is dry, Koi fish are moved to another pond in the garden. Now fund raising in progress to restore the garden.

In spite of this it is still a nice place to visit in San Jose.<//review>

< Text>
This is a fairly large friendship garden with a lot to see. There are plenty of places to sit and watch the pond or greenery, and it's good for couples, friends, or families. It doesn't have the authenticity or grandeur of some other Japanese Gardens (eg: the one in San Francisco's Golden Gate Park), but this one is free, so that explains some of the trade-offs. I would appreciate a tea house or other shop being open in the park (It looked like there may have been one that was closed?), but it's great in its current form too.< /Text>
